  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer5861455524892807024">Breaking the laws of nature is a serious crime!<br/><br/>In an alchemical ritual gone wrong, Edward Elric lost his arm and his leg, and his brother Alphonse became nothing but a soul in a suit of armor. Equipped with mechanical “auto-mail” limbs, Edward becomes a state alchemist, seeking the one thing that can restore his and his brother’s bodies...the legendary Philosopher’s Stone.</span>
  <span id="freeText5861455524892807024" style="display:none">Breaking the laws of nature is a serious crime!<br /><br />In an alchemical ritual gone wrong, Edward Elric lost his arm and his leg, and his brother Alphonse became nothing but a soul in a suit of armor. Equipped with mechanical “auto-mail” limbs, Edward becomes a state alchemist, seeking the one thing that can restore his and his brother’s bodies...the legendary Philosopher’s Stone.<br /><br />Alchemy: the mystical power to alter the natural world; something between magic, art and science. When two brothers, Edward and Alphonse Elric, dabbled in this power to grant their dearest wish, one of them lost an arm and a leg…and the other became nothing but a soul locked into a body of living steel. Now Edward is an agent of the government, a slave of the military-alchemical complex, using his unique powers to obey orders…even to kill. Except his powers aren't unique. The world has been ravaged by the abuse of alchemy. And in pursuit of the ultimate alchemical treasure, the Philosopher's Stone, their enemies are even more ruthless than they are…</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/491590-is-this-book-a-manga-or-not-because-it">is this book a manga or not because it looks like a manga and im not a big fan of those it said I would like it because I rate harry potter but if its a manga I don&#39;t want to read it?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_491590'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F870.Fullmetal_Alchemist_Vol_1">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/491590-is-this-book-a-manga-or-not-because-it">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/491590-is-this-book-a-manga-or-not-because-it">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/14337440-cressie-patterson"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1352253647i/14337440._UY100_CR20,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/14337440-cressie-patterson">Cressie Patterson</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes, Fullmetal Alchemist is a manga, which tells its story through drawn artwork and dialogue, but this one is relatively shorter than most popular sh<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes, Fullmetal Alchemist is a manga, which tells its story through drawn artwork and dialogue, but this one is relatively shorter than most popular shonen series. FMA finished up with 27 manga volumes. It was such a hugely popular series, it also spawned five novels as well, so you could read those if you didn't want to try your hand at manga. The first Fullmetal Alchemist novel is called "The Land of Sand". You can find them on Ebay. <br /><br />It's kind of odd that you were prompted to read Fullmetal Alchemist if you like Harry Potter but don't have an interest in manga. Most likely because of the link that both series have to the Philosopher's Stone, but they don't really have that much else in common. Well, I'd say that Edward Elric, the main hero character in FMA is even more altruistic than Harry Potter, and both series have over-the-top villains that want to take over the world, but the FMA story is darker, in it's own way, than Harry Potter. Still, because of the common link between the two series, crossover fanfictions between Harry Potter &amp; FMA are very popular on fanfic websites. Both series boast casts of incredibly colorful and likable characters, both have unforgettable storylines, and both series have spawned incredibly popular theme park attractions at Universal Studios Parks, HP currently, and FMA used to have one in Japan. <br /><br />If you can't get into reading manga, you should try watching the FMA anime series. The first one, made in 2003, follows the author's story only halfway through the series, then the anime production crew made up their own ending to finish the series, seeing as the manga's creator was still in the middle of her story. The second series, Fullmetal Alchemist: Brotherhood, made in 2009, follows the original manga storyline more faithfully until the end, although it does rush through the early details of the series, since they were already known to the fans from watching the first series.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1232668470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7330459079508370590">I have no idea what, in this manga, prompted an average rating of 4.47/5 stars. No idea. It's even higher than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13615.Death_Note__Vol__1_Boredom__Death_Note___1_' title='Death Note, Vol. 1 Boredom (Death Note, #1) by Tsugumi Ohba' rel='nofollow noopener'>Death Note, Vol. 1: Boredom</a> (which is the most read manga on GR) and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2454986.Fairy_Tail__Vol__01__Fairy_Tail___1_' title='Fairy Tail, Vol. 01 (Fairy Tail, #1) by Hiro Mashima' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fairy Tail, Vol. 01</a> which, until it became too repetitive, used to be my F-A-V-O-R-I-T-E manga series. Because the characters and drawings and world-building are extraordinary.<br/><br/>Nonetheless, the world-building in this book too wasn't bad either. But there were too many characters that appeared and then disappeared... no </span>
  <span id="freeText7330459079508370590" style="display:none">I have no idea what, in this manga, prompted an average rating of 4.47/5 stars. No idea. It's even higher than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13615.Death_Note__Vol__1_Boredom__Death_Note___1_" title="Death Note, Vol. 1 Boredom (Death Note, #1) by Tsugumi Ohba" rel="nofollow noopener">Death Note, Vol. 1: Boredom</a> (which is the most read manga on GR) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2454986.Fairy_Tail__Vol__01__Fairy_Tail___1_" title="Fairy Tail, Vol. 01 (Fairy Tail, #1) by Hiro Mashima" rel="nofollow noopener">Fairy Tail, Vol. 01</a> which, until it became too repetitive, used to be my F-A-V-O-R-I-T-E manga series. Because the characters and drawings and world-building are extraordinary.<br /><br />Nonetheless, the world-building in this book too wasn't bad either. But there were too many characters that appeared and then disappeared... no time to get attached. This is something that I think can be interesting but NOT in a first volume! Edward and his brother, however, were fun to follow on their ''adventures''. There was a good enough backstory but too short! Very little detail! I'm going to assume, though, that there will be more in the sequels. <br /><br />The premise was something I enjoyed too. Too many ''cases'' (problems) to resolve - I would prefer one but long, deep and poignant - but just the fact that there were alchemists in the storyline was something unique and I wish to discover more about them.<br /><br />I will continue with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7330459079508370590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1939183144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1939183144" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1939183144?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen/The Tolkien Gal/ジェニファー" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen/The Tolkien Gal/ジェニファー" href="/user/show/4919283-jen-the-tolkien-gal">Jen/The Tolkien Gal/ジェニファー</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4919283-jen-the-tolkien-gal?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4919283-jen-the-tolkien-gal?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4919283-jen-the-tolkien-gal?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4919283-jen-the-tolkien-gal?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1939183144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2364266764546866861">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31153167-bhavik' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bhavik</a><br/>It's my first time reading this series and I'm hyped!<br/><br/>Looking forward to this so much, friend!<br/><br/>I've decided to review each volume by chapter, as each chapter has an underlying theme that can't be ignored. Also, it's mostly me rambling and fangirling so I apologise in advance. Compared to most of my "articulate" reviews, these will be a jumbled mess.<br/><br/><b>"The Two Alchemists" (二人の錬金術師 Futari no Renkinjutsushi) - containing one of the most memorable anime scenes of my childhood </b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819321._SY540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819322.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>"If y</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2364266764546866861" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31153167-bhavik" rel="nofollow noopener">Bhavik</a><br>It's my first time reading this series and I'm hyped!<br><br>Looking forward to this so much, friend!<br><br>I've decided to review each volume by chapter, as each chapter has an underlying theme that can't be ignored. Also, it's mostly me rambling and fangirling so I apologise in advance. Compared to most of my "articulate" reviews, these will be a jumbled mess.<br><br><b>"The Two Alchemists" (二人の錬金術師 Futari no Renkinjutsushi) - containing one of the most memorable anime scenes of my childhood </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819321._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819322.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"If you have enough faith, you'll definitely get bigger."</i><br><br><br>This is the volume where we are introduced to Alphonse and Edward - the Elric brothers. And boy it's such a fantastic introduction.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819323.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A little background of the world if you haven't watched/read FMA: Think if the industrial revolution took place with alchemy (a type of magic where different elements can be manipulated). This chapter is all about corrupted religious institutions and their effect on people. <br><br>I can't wait to be introduced to old favourites, but for now just seeing the brothers again is a treat. Still love that everyone assumes Alphonse is older. Edward's height often gets made fun of, which is always so much fun to read and watch.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819324.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819325._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So there's this asshole called Cornello who belongs to the house of the sun god, Leto. Cornello reportedly has the philosopher's ring, a ring of restoration - a ring that can bring people back from the dead.<br><br>Rose is an innocent girl who helps Cornello so that she can get her boyfriend back with the power of the philosopher's stone. After seeing my friend just lose her boyfriend so tragically and at such a young light, (and having a boyfriend of four years) I finally understand Rose's desperation. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819326._SY540_.png" alt="Image result for cornello fullmetal alchemist manga" width="230" height="353" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I love love love about this chapter is that it critcises the hubris of both religious people and atheists. It shows that no matter what our beliefs, we can all be asses and holier-than-thou about it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819327.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819328.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hiromu Arakawa is such a great writer! She shows that there is wisdom in the young and naivety in the old. <br><br>Minor spoiler: The chapter ends with the reveal of Ed's arm and the whole scene is glorious.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529407790i/25819329._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> "The Price of Life" (命の代価 Inochi no Daika)</b><br><br>I find out funny how Cornello thinks that Ed has committed the greatest sin <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the sin of human transmutation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> what Cornello is doing is so much worse, especially given his age compared to when Ed did what he did. How can you blame two young boys for missing their mother after their father has walked out on them? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829082._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fullmetal Alchemist understands the importance of having the right balance of text and images in a comic. It's busy, but it doesn't bust your brain and give you a comic-induced headache. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829083._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Al and Ed are just yin an yang - the fierce and gentle one, the proud and quiet one. I just love them. I love how they support each other on the road they have chosen - it's do or die to get their bodies back.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829084._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's rare in any story where the characters start out with a burden and a sacrifice - many new books have a character who only picks up a burden on the way. But this is why FMA is such a gem. I also love that Ed doesn't stop Cornello with alchemy, but with wits.<br><br>Also, how could you not love Ed's facial expressions?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829085.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ooh and do I love a good story that doesn't end in forgiveness but death instead. Forgive me, but I'm petty like that.<br><br>And what Ed says to Rose...powerful stuff.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829086._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829087._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Also a lovely introduction to some of the main villains is in order...<br><br><b>Chapter 3: "The Mining Town" (炭鉱の街 Tankō no Machi)</b><br><br>Since I've only watched the original anime series, a lot of this is uncharted territory from here on out for me. So I'm so excited!<br><br>A lot of good humour in this one. It also really highlights the prejudice against the alchemist military. I love how militia corruption is the main theme in this chapter, where previous chapters dealt with religious corruption. It shows the good and bad side of military members. Yoki is such an ass - he treats those below him badly but is a total sycophant to those above him.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829088.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"Kid, you don't get it. This is our home and our coffin."<br><br>This is such a good chapter that introduces us to the heart that Ed and Al have in helping others. They give so much, despite what they've lost.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829089._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829090.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Chapter 4: "Battle on the Train" (車上の戦い Shajō no Tatakai)</b><br><br>Crimes are being committed on trains by a bunch called the "blue group".<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829091.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WE GET INTRODUCED TO HAWKEYE AND MUSTANG AND THE GANG. Peeps, it's getting real.<br><br>I'm Roy's number one fan, so everyone else can just move out the way please. IT"S MY ROYBOY<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829092.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alright - back to the story. So Ed and Al end up on one of the trains that the Blue Group is going to steal from. What the Blue Group doesn't know is that they picked the wrong hostages. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829093.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ah, Alphonse. Always taking control while Ed kicks ass. &lt;3 My boys. Al gets to shine a little in this one.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829094.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After reading the 4th chapter, I can't help but think that each bad guy in every chapter of this volume represents some kind of greed - and we all know that greed (and Greed) plays a huge role in this manga. In this volume, it's pirate guy. (I didn't pick up on his name)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529563472i/25829095.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Closing comments:</b> I still believe that FMA is one of the most beautifully stylised manga in history. Also, this first volume shows us that although the philosopher's stone is the ultimate goal of our brothers, they never cease to help others along the way. We also get introduced to the Roy-Ed dynamic, which has always been one of my favourites. <br><br>All-in-all, this is a fullmetal start to my buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31153167-bhavik" rel="nofollow noopener">Bhavik</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3504267803" />
    <a title="Lauren Lanz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82987361-lauren-lanz"><img alt="Lauren Lanz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586150400p2/82987361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3504267803?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Lanz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Lanz" href="/user/show/82987361-lauren-lanz">Lauren Lanz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=author-of-colour">author-of-colour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3504267803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11654838514954642311">One of my good friends (in reference to <i>Fullmetal Alchemist</i>) once told me: <b>Literally every other manga, ever, should take notes.</b><br/><br/>WOW was he right. Edward and Alphonse stole my heart from the get-go; the overarching story left me eager for more. I’ll be damned if I can’t get my hands on the next volume soon! <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Nothing's perfect, the world's not perfect. But it's there for us, trying the best it can; that's what makes it so damn beautiful.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>
  <u>~★~ What is this book about? ~★~</u>
</b><br/><br/>Young Edward and Alp</span>
  <span id="freeText11654838514954642311" style="display:none">One of my good friends (in reference to <i>Fullmetal Alchemist</i>) once told me: <b>Literally every other manga, ever, should take notes.</b><br /><br />WOW was he right. Edward and Alphonse stole my heart from the get-go; the overarching story left me eager for more. I’ll be damned if I can’t get my hands on the next volume soon! <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Nothing's perfect, the world's not perfect. But it's there for us, trying the best it can; that's what makes it so damn beautiful.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>~★~ What is this book about? ~★~</u>
</b><br /><br />Young Edward and Alphonse wanted nothing more than to see their dead mother again. They attempt to resurrect her with alchemy (a craft that allows wielders to alter matter using equal give and take), except their wish is too grand, and things go awry. Dabbling in dangerous power has left Edward without an arm and a leg, and Alphonse missing his body entirely--soul bound to an empty suit of armor. Together, the brothers are searching for a stone that can amplify alchemy in the hopes of getting their original bodies back.<br /><br />~★~ <br /><br />This was honestly such a great time! <i>Fullmetal Alchemist</i> immediately drew me in with its plentiful action and wit. Alphonse and Edward--our protagonists--were probably the most enticing factors for me. It’s been a while since I’ve encountered characters like them, whom I come to love immediately upon meeting.<br /><br />Hiromu Arakawa’s art style was in my eyes near perfect. The clean lines and overall character concepts were right up my alley in terms of personal preference. My sister flipped through the pages, marvelling at the neat art style, too!<br /><br />There isn’t much else to say besides the fact that this manga more than exceeded my expectations. Knowing that this is only the first cusp of the story leaves me extremely excited for what’s to come!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11654838514954642311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_92385223" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92385223" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92385223?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=fangirl-alert">fangirl-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92385223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14638469885028147211">Love love love love love.<br/><br/><br/>It's actually been quite some time since I first read this volume, and now that my public library has finally started buying the series (just in time for me to leave town - thanks, guys) I checked out the first seven on a whim. <br/><br/>I'd actually forgotten a lot about this volume. Somehow I got the idea that the Cornello/Liore plot was stretched over the entire volume, and that Youswell was in V. 2, and obviously that was wrong - and the train thing I'd forgotten entirely. It </span>
  <span id="freeText14638469885028147211" style="display:none">Love love love love love.<br /><br /><br />It's actually been quite some time since I first read this volume, and now that my public library has finally started buying the series (just in time for me to leave town - thanks, guys) I checked out the first seven on a whim. <br /><br />I'd actually forgotten a lot about this volume. Somehow I got the idea that the Cornello/Liore plot was stretched over the entire volume, and that Youswell was in V. 2, and obviously that was wrong - and the train thing I'd forgotten entirely. It was interesting to go back, too, and compare the art and plotting of this volume to that of the very end. Obviously, there is significant improvement, but the seeds of - dare I say it? Yes, I do - <b>greatness to come</b> are definitely here. In much the same way as a webcomic artist develops over time, the art and plotting improve as the series goes on, but this first entry is the furthest thing from shabby.<br /><br />So anyhow, this volume. Yes. Youswell is my favorite plotline in it, possibly my favorite episodic entry in the series as a whole, because it really shows Ed's integrity as a character. I mean, all three plotlines do that, though the train one is not as good as the others just because its main purpose is to segue into an introduction of Mustang and Co. Youswell is still the best. It establishes so many things for the rest of the series - the idea of corruption in the military, Ed's renegade attitude, his almost instinctual commitment to doing the right thing no matter what, and more. It's really kind of amazing to look back on these first few chapters and wonder what Arakawa was thinking - I'd love to know how it is to work in manga publishing. Surely when she was writing/drawing these, she couldn't have imagined the massive success that would follow. What was she planning? The whole thing? And what a tragedy it would have been if the series had been canceled before it could run its full arc. (I assume this can happen in manga; it's only logical.)<br /><br />I remember reading this for the first time and being interested but at the same time put off by the episodic style, which I expected to be the norm for the entire series. If anyone else out there has that niggling worry, be not afraid: fairly quickly, a full arc asserts itself and it'll sweep you up entirely.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Original rambling fangirly review under the spoiler tags - no actual spoilers.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[EDIT:<br /><br />So, I have this theory. Your first lengthy manga series is like your first Doctor Who. (Eccleston doesn't count; he's more like a short manga.) There is a certain undying loyalty that goes with it. For me, my first Doctor was Matt Smith. (Except for the aforementioned Eccleston; I did see the second episode of the first series and 'The Empty Child' before I saw 'The Eleventh Hour'.) Ergo, my loyalty as a viewer is to Smith, in defiance of all the rabid Tennant fans out there.<br />In the same way, FMA was my first long manga. And really, I don't think anything will ever top it for me. What are you looking for in your story today? Would you like some kickass magic? How about an elegant and thorough plot? How about deep questions and powerful themes? And perhaps a side of laughs? And with all that, as a bonus, we'll throw in a gang of strong heroines to make up for the lack in much American YA.<br />I'm glad I read this when I did, since I think it partly got me through my AP Chemistry homework. But I also envy those who get to read it now that it's completed. Seriously, those last few chapters had me on tenterhooks for weeks.<br /><br /><br /><br />I'll admit, I was surprised at how dang much I enjoy this series. But the story's really well done- enough drama, horror, humour and just plain AWESOMENESS to keep me intrigued and on my guard.<br />I've started watching the anime now, and I'm not wild about how they're rearranging the chronology; otherwise, both versions are good.<br /><br />***<br /><br />Okay, so at this point I'm about 3/4 of the way through the 2003 anime- I'll get to Brotherhood this summer, I swear!- and I'm really confusing myself. So a note- while it does help to have read the manga when watching the anime, do not do this concurrent. Because things go one way in the manga and another in the anime and it gets so baffling sometimes. I have to quiz someone who's seen/read both to get things straight- who's Bradley in this one, who's dead, what happens where/when, etc.<br /><br />I don't understand how anyone would prefer the anime to the manga, honestly. The manga's much more complex and interesting to me; the anime's condensed and loses some of the subtler characterization, sub-plots, and world development Arakawa put in.<br /><br />***<br /><br />I WILL NOT RANT ABOUT THE SHITTY ENDING OF THE ANIME. I WILL NOT. I WILL NOT COMPLAIN ABOUT THE SHANNARA-ESQUE EPIC COPOUT. I WON'T, I WON'T, I WON'T.<br /><br />***<br /><br />In other news:<br />Gah, I am in so much love with this series. I'm going to get caught up this week. 106 is on OneManga, so it's certainly possible.<br />Particularly happy with:<br />Everything in the north, pretty much. Briggs ftw. I imagine myself there. Though I'd totally die. And zOMG, I'd steal Ed's fur-lined coat. FUZZY!<br />Manga Sloth has so much Slothness on anime Sloth.<br />Is it bad that I kind of like Gluttony? As a character, not fangirling, but I think he's funny and kind of charming in a really friggin dangerous little kid way.<br />I love Arakawa's extras. Especially Riza and the Pride-stickers. I lol'd so hard.<br />I've spent far too much time looking up fanart for this on DeviantArt. Especially Royai. Definitely an OTP. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="14638469885028147211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jokoloyo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jokoloyo" href="/user/show/1902630-jokoloyo">Jokoloyo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124819031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3735313487838894102">I highly recommend this manga for hard magic system fantasy fans who don't read manga. Full Metal Alchemist (FMA) manga has many strong points as a fantasy story:<br/>1. The setting/world building is rich. It has steampunk taste (showing a lot of highly advanced mechanical prosthetic limbs), First World War era, and magical alchemist system.<br/><br/>2. I am not an expert in <a href='http://brandonsanderson.com/article/40/Sandersons-First-Law' rel='nofollow noopener'> Sanderson's First Law </a> but after I read the article, I believe this manga can be considered as a Hard Magic system story. The magic syst</span>
  <span id="freeText3735313487838894102" style="display:none">I highly recommend this manga for hard magic system fantasy fans who don't read manga. Full Metal Alchemist (FMA) manga has many strong points as a fantasy story:<br />1. The setting/world building is rich. It has steampunk taste (showing a lot of highly advanced mechanical prosthetic limbs), First World War era, and magical alchemist system.<br /><br />2. I am not an expert in <a href="http://brandonsanderson.com/article/40/Sandersons-First-Law" rel="nofollow noopener"> Sanderson's First Law </a> but after I read the article, I believe this manga can be considered as a Hard Magic system story. The magic system is clearly explained and when the story progressing, the author can deliver many non-cheating plot twists with the rules of alchemist.<br /><br />3. Tons of sympathetic characters. In my opinion, this manga has the largest amount of sympathetic minor characters in manga. The author design many minor characters to give impact to the story. I don't want to spoil much, but one of my friends said the FMA won't be this good without character X and Y (I won't spoil the names. I hope you have your own favorite characters when reading this manga).<br /><br />4. In my opinion, the plot is flawless from beginning to the end. I am afraid if I elaborate more I will spoil some fun.<br /><br />5. This manga is not a comedy story, but there are some light moments. The humor is pretty evenly spread until the end. That means the author could keep the balance of humour better than most of humour/comedy mangas.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3735313487838894102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14789505856794789504"><b>2 Stars </b> <br/><br/>Um.... Am I missing something??<br/><br/>This series has a super high average (4.49 as I write this) and several of my friends have really enjoyed it. But I was just very underwhelmed? <br/><br/>This is <i>incredibly</i> creative, both the magical aspect and the brothers being the way they are. The brothers were both fun characters and their loyalty to each other was enjoyable.<br/><br/>But I wish this world had been explained a little more before they just started embarking on all these different adventures. It sort of fe</span>
  <span id="freeText14789505856794789504" style="display:none"><b>2 Stars </b> <br /><br />Um.... Am I missing something??<br /><br />This series has a super high average (4.49 as I write this) and several of my friends have really enjoyed it. But I was just very underwhelmed? <br /><br />This is <i>incredibly</i> creative, both the magical aspect and the brothers being the way they are. The brothers were both fun characters and their loyalty to each other was enjoyable.<br /><br />But I wish this world had been explained a little more before they just started embarking on all these different adventures. It sort of feels like they are just going to wonder town to town and keep getting in trouble. Not only was the large cast of side characters kind of annoying, but there didn't seem to be much of an overreaching plot. <br /><br />I know lots of people love this series, but it's just not for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14789505856794789504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1530045662" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1530045662" />
    <a title="Lily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1899725-lily"><img alt="Lily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451003929p2/1899725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1530045662?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lily" href="/user/show/1899725-lily">Lily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1899725-lily?shelf=books-with-pictures">books-with-pictures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1899725-lily?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1899725-lily?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1899725-lily?shelf=2016-2017-goals">2016-2017-goals</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1530045662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17033813929228382483">3.5 stars *flips coin to decide whether to round up or down*<br/><br/>Of all the stages of grief, "bargaining" has always struck me as the most interesting and memorable: the appraisal of all we have and don't have, and the hypothetical transactions that we think would make things better. It's an activity whose allure is counterbalanced by its low probability of success. What would the world be like if bargaining actually had some chance of working? That's the world of <i>Fullmetal Alchemist</i>. <br/><br/>Following the d</span>
  <span id="freeText17033813929228382483" style="display:none">3.5 stars *flips coin to decide whether to round up or down*<br /><br />Of all the stages of grief, "bargaining" has always struck me as the most interesting and memorable: the appraisal of all we have and don't have, and the hypothetical transactions that we think would make things better. It's an activity whose allure is counterbalanced by its low probability of success. What would the world be like if bargaining actually had some chance of working? That's the world of <i>Fullmetal Alchemist</i>. <br /><br />Following the death of their mother, the brothers Edward and Alphonse engage in an alchemical ritual that seems guaranteed to bring her back. They fail, but that's not the worst of it; in the process, Edward loses a limb and Alphonse loses his whole body, left as a soul inhabiting a hollow suit of armor. We follow them as they attempt to put their lives and bodies back together, encountering other, dangerous alchemists along the way. <br /><br />This first volume is very episodic, covering three stories that seem pretty independent of each other. The first story, which I think was the longest of the three, was my favorite. It's about the vulnerability of people who want to retrieve the irretrievable, and it shows what the brothers learned from their own attempts at doing that. The art is cleverly done; sometimes the most effective way to convey a horrible image is to barely show the edge of it and leave the rest up to reader/viewer imagination, and here it's done to great effect. <br /><br />Though, this volume as a whole isn't super serious. In the preface, Hiromu Arakawa talks about her fondness for B-movies and how she wanted to create a similar effect in this manga, and I think she succeeded at that. There are a lot of hilarious, over-the-top action scenes, and I love when humor comes through in the art style and people suddenly turn into freaked-out stick figures. However, action scenes don't hold my attention for very long, and I ultimately didn't find those parts of the story to be particularly memorable. <br /><br />Nonetheless, I'm excited to continue with the series and I'm looking forward to seeing some kind of continual story-arc emerge. The story has an interesting magic system, with real power coming at real cost. More importantly, it has a big heart. And Alphonse is adorable. More please!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17033813929228382483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_5313589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5313589" />
    <a title="Lizziegolightly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/303792-lizziegolightly"><img alt="Lizziegolightly" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5313589?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lizziegolightly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lizziegolightly" href="/user/show/303792-lizziegolightly">Lizziegolightly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/303792-lizziegolightly?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5313589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17877929118420853227"><i> Fullmetal Alchemist </i> in its anime form is one of my favorite television shows. I watch it religiously, even now that I have seen every episode. I never read manga before and basically, I picked up this edition because of my devotion to the program. <br/><br/>This first installment of the manga is damn near close to (if not completely) identical to the first few episodes of the show. I won't give away the plot twists, just for those of you who haven't seen it yet. The essential storyline, though, is that </span>
  <span id="freeText17877929118420853227" style="display:none"><i> Fullmetal Alchemist </i> in its anime form is one of my favorite television shows. I watch it religiously, even now that I have seen every episode. I never read manga before and basically, I picked up this edition because of my devotion to the program. <br /><br />This first installment of the manga is damn near close to (if not completely) identical to the first few episodes of the show. I won't give away the plot twists, just for those of you who haven't seen it yet. The essential storyline, though, is that brothers Ed and Al attempt to use alchemy to bring back their mother from the dead. Instead, Ed loses some limbs and Al loses his whole body. Despite the fact that Al's soul is encased in a suit of armor, Ed is actually the Fullmetal Alchemist (I think "Fullmetal" is a translation of Japanese slang for pigheaded). Ed ends up working for the military and Al comes along with him and the ultimate hope is that, while working as alchemists, they can find the Philosopher's Stone that will hopefully restore their bodies.<br /><br />The theme of the series is Equivalent Exchange, the idea that in order to gain something, one must give up something of equal value. It's something I believe as truth even in the world of non-alchemists, so perhaps that's why I'm drawn to this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17877929118420853227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97668249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97668249" />
    <a title="King Haddock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1469669-king-haddock"><img alt="King Haddock" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435161176p2/1469669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97668249?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="King Haddock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="King Haddock" href="/user/show/1469669-king-haddock">King Haddock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1469669-king-haddock?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1469669-king-haddock?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1469669-king-haddock?shelf=reviews-with-some-depth">reviews-with-some-depth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1469669-king-haddock?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1469669-king-haddock?shelf=fandom">fandom</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97668249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2177786490637501575">I have become a skeptical reader over the years. It's because I've read A LOT. I was the kid who could read over 12,000 pages in a single summer - and I know because I counted. So I learned about plots, characterization, and all the things authors can do to make reading a pleasant experience.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, after a while, you become so knowledgeable of the meta-world that you lose sight of the treasure within the tale. Frequently I pick up a fantasy or science-fiction novel off a shelf and think,</span>
  <span id="freeText2177786490637501575" style="display:none">I have become a skeptical reader over the years. It's because I've read A LOT. I was the kid who could read over 12,000 pages in a single summer - and I know because I counted. So I learned about plots, characterization, and all the things authors can do to make reading a pleasant experience.<br /><br />Unfortunately, after a while, you become so knowledgeable of the meta-world that you lose sight of the treasure within the tale. Frequently I pick up a fantasy or science-fiction novel off a shelf and think, "This looks exactly like everything else."<br /><br />But. Fullmetal Alchemist. blew. me. away.<br /><br />As you can tell from my previous reviews of this first book (I kept them below... but I felt the need to rewrite this review YET AGAIN, sorry everyone), it took me a little bit of time to get into the series. It was good, but it didn't stand out to me too much at first. Books one and two didn't excite me all that much, and in fact I was a little offended by some of the content. Maybe you don't have that problem, but if you do share my lack of "hm, it's okay," just keep reading. <br /><br />Hiromu Arakawa created a world of alchemy, something that makes me want to be an alchemist because it's just so amazing. She wrote in characters with heart-wrenching back stories and wonderful personalities. I have developed a strong opinion of every single character in the series, something that few authors can really get me to do. We've got an incredible cast with wide personalities, and they're all so incredibly distinct. I squeal over Armstrong, squeal over Mustang and Hawkeye, and most of all, squeal over the relationship between Edward and Alphonse.<br /><br />There are two things that make this series absolutely fantastic beyond belief, and the first is the brothers and emotional depth we see there. The relationship between Ed and Al is incredibly poignant, heart-breaking, and heart-warming. They have gone through an incredible amount in their lives, and you feel it just as strongly as they do. I don't know that I could be any more invested in characters than this. We see loyalty, love, and perseverance. How Ed defends Al gets me every time.<br /><br />This brings me to the second incredible thing that distinguishes FMA from anything else I have read: the depth in the story. We aren't just in for action (though we've got a lot of that), romance (though there's certainly the "aww" moments), humor (though I always crack up), or plot twists (though Arakawa is ingenious in plot progression). We get a whole set of deep questions. The characters aren't just alchemists - they ask WHY they do it, if it's worth doing it, when it's worth doing it, what they should do with it. WMorals come up everywhere - when is it okay to kill people, if ever? How should we deal with sacrifice? How do we treat human souls? When does someone stop becoming human? We're bashed with questions over sacrifice, genocide, utilitarianism versus deontology... You don't just have an adventure when you read FMA, you have a real experience that leads you away changed and... in my case... absolutely obsessed.<br /><br />More comments about FMA can be found in my other reviews. You can even check out the first half of #27 to see my reaction when I completed the series (I give a warning before I start on volume-specific comments).<br /><br />Happy reading.<br /><br />----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><br />I decided to reread the first two volumes of Fullmetal Alchemist because:<br />1. I hadn't read them in a while<br />2. I plan to continue reading the series about now<br />3. The library didn't have book three in.<br /><br />So. As a second read-through, I would say the series is much better. In fact, I just bumped it up from three to four stars. Or maybe it's because I read the book in slightly a different light.<br /><br />The first two books contain a lot of philosophical analysis concerning religion. I do not inherently consider this a bad thing; contrarily, the first two chapters in which a very cult-like society is realistically formed intrigued me during my re-read. I mean, it has all the standards one might psychologically expect: a strong, egotistic leader whom everyone follows without question, the claims of being a direct representative from God, a closed community, a desire for power amongst the authorities, etc. So that was sort of fun to analyze. But then - to continue onto book two (I might as well when on this train of thought) - we meet Scar, who even uses some possible vague scriptural references such as "there is a time to create and to destroy." Now, I do not have a problem with those sorts of psycho-religious bad guys, but I think one thing that got me disjointed at the beginning of FMA is the seemingly constant negative religious spin. Maybe that's me, maybe that's just the first two books... I don't know. It's not that Hiromu Arakawa does not have valid points concerning religions' dangerous facets, it's just very flinchingly one-sided at the moment.<br /><br />To clarify that ramble: maybe that's why I rated the first book three stars at first.<br /><br />Now let's get onto the good stuff. Rereading it, I found a bit more enjoyment in the dialogue and personality of the characters (first reread, it took me until book two to get the hang of it all). And there are some interesting moral questions brought up in this series that I find intriguing... a lot of teleological versus deontological issues, some I would have solved differently, but still fun to read. And the alchemy setting is well-done, particularly about the cost of trying to transmute humans. Very nice.<br /><br />I think it's hard to review manga based on just the first volume, so I think my opinions will become more relevant the further along I go in the series. Which, so I hope, will be further than book two this go-round!<br /><br />----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br />Original review:<br /><br />As a first book in a series, it doesn't really particularly stand out - except that you can see a lot of potential where it is going. The second book of the series is where I started to really get into the storyline (because this one, like many first books, is such an introduction you can't really claim too much of a significant storyline). </span>
  <a data-text-id="2177786490637501575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review97668249">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2282574840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8261009891584547158">Not really blown away, but it is a great start for Fullmetal Alchemist! It is a great teaser for everything you will expect from the series. Hiromu Arakawa has perfectly set the pace and the amount of humor and action in the story. As early as now, I can see why this is one of the best rated manga series in history.<br/><br/>Volume 1 establishes the foundations of a terrific tale of the Alchemist brothers and I am very excited to be in this crazy, fun (and at times endearing) manga ride.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1912219714939362069">I first saw this series on Netflix. Let me just say I watched almost all of the episodes till <i>Netflix</i> <s>assholes</s> took out seasons two and three for <b>NO REASON</b>.<br/><br/>I love this series! Not my first anime I've fell in love with but I of course fell in love with the characters anyways, two brothers, Edward and Alphonse Elric.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438120040ra/15666949.gif' width='270' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438120235ra/15666960.gif' width='270' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/></span>
  <span id="freeText1912219714939362069" style="display:none">I first saw this series on Netflix. <div id="review_3547656358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3547656358" />
    <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello"><img alt="Michael Sorbello" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521124600p2/4307906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3547656358?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Sorbello" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello">Michael Sorbello</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=all-comics">all-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=instagram">instagram</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3547656358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer959382331206179563">This is a review of the entire series.<br/><br/>Fullmetal Alchemist takes place in the fictional country of Amestris which is heavily based on the Industrial Revolution. Amestris is a unitary state under the rule of a parliamentary republic, run by state alchemists that serve the king utilizing the mystifying arts of alchemy. Alchemy is the power to alter the physical world utilizing its natural elements, performing magic and miracles in the form of science. Alchemy follows the law of equivalent exchange,</span>
  <span id="freeText959382331206179563" style="display:none">This is a review of the entire series.<br /><br />Fullmetal Alchemist takes place in the fictional country of Amestris which is heavily based on the Industrial Revolution. Amestris is a unitary state under the rule of a parliamentary republic, run by state alchemists that serve the king utilizing the mystifying arts of alchemy. Alchemy is the power to alter the physical world utilizing its natural elements, performing magic and miracles in the form of science. Alchemy follows the law of equivalent exchange, you must sacrifice something that is of equal value to what you create. You must sacrifice a life to create a life, you must extinguish one flame to ignite another, you have to sacrifice one home to build another, etc...<br /><br />After being abandoned by their father as children and subjected to watching their mother die, Edward Elric and his brother Alphonse once attempted to utilize the power of alchemy to bring their mother back from the grave, ignoring the dangers of creating a life by offering something of equal value. Edward loses an arm and a leg while Alphonse loses his entire body; his soul placed in a hollow suit of armor that can't feel the touch of others. As neither of them sacrificed their lives in their entirety, the exchange failed and the boys created an abomination in place of their dead mother.<br /><br />After burning their own home down and dealing with the abomination they created, Edward and his brother enlist themselves in the military to atone for their sins and learn more about the many secrets of alchemy; potentially learning how to recover their original bodies in the process. While serving in the military, the brothers begin to realize how the wonders of alchemy can be abused for nefarious purposes. Immortal life can be gained by sacrificing hundreds of innocents souls, wars can be staged and foreign nations can be annihilated under false charges, human experimentation aided by alchemy can lead to unnatural mutations, the world of alchemy is more dark and dangerous than either of them could've bargained for.<br /><br />Fullmetal Alchemist grew on me the longer I read it. When I first started reading, it seemed like it was going to be generic shounen material, but it gets deeper and darker the further it goes on. The way it handles political and religious corruption, the dangers of advanced states abusing their technology and resources at the expense of foreign nations caught in the turmoil, and the sad futility of revenge are all very well done.<br /><br />The characters all bear the weight of what alchemy is capable of. Edward and Alphonse carry the burden of abusing alchemy for selfish purposes. Their master Izumi loses her womb after attempting to resurrect her dead child. Scar takes many lives after his entire country is desecrated and gets trapped in a pointless cycle of revenge. Roy and Riza endure the regret of committing brutal war crimes for the sake of protecting their own nation. Alchemy creates and destroys in equal measure and no one is free from the consequences of tipping the balance.<br /><br />The fight scenes are flashy and exciting without being too over-the-top because of the dangerous limitations that alchemy involves. The law of equivalent exchange keeps the power scaling in check and adds plenty of tension to the action. The female characters are especially well done, all of them are strong and unique in their own way. The lead heroine Winry being a skilled mechanic, Riza being an honorable warrior of the military, Olivier Armstrong as cold and vicious as the snowy fortress she guards, and that's just a few of them.<br /><br />The villains are an interesting parody of the seven deadly sins. Each of them represent the darkness and regrets of each of the main characters and they can only be conquered by coming to terms with their own flaws and sins. The characters having to overcome their personal demons to take on the greater demons trying to overthrow the world from the shadows made the struggles of every single person in the story feel personal. Every character, no matter how minor had their moments to shine. Everyone had a vital role to play and the camaraderie between friend and foe alike never felt cheesy or forced.<br /><br />Unlike most shounen series I've read, the final arc was my favorite. A lot of long-running shounen series have a habit of being dragged out, losing touch with what made them great or breaking their own rules in messy, plot-hole-filled final arcs that leave a lot to be desired. Fullmetal Alchemist has no lose ends, all characters have complete arcs where they learn and grow from their dark pasts, the romance and comedy are handled well without relying on cheap fanservice, the action scenes are great but they don't overshadow the plot and the final chapters tie everything together beautifully. It's not my favorite manga by any means as I usually tend to favor seinen, but it's definitely one of the greatest stories to ever come out of the shounen demographic in my opinion. The ending is a tearjerker but it left me in good spirits.<br /><br />***<br /><br />My Social Media<br /><br />My Instagram Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/michael_sorbello/">https://www.instagram.com/michael_sor...</a><br /><br />My YouTube Channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs1eOzsOqcz5ey5JjGSbg">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs...</a><br /><br />My Wattpad Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-Sorbello">https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-...</a><br /><br />My Twitter Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror">https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror</a><br /><br />My Facebook Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorbello.104">https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorb...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="959382331206179563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776580197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9304090608021895180"> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479049135i/21142615.jpg' width='800' height='600' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Even if you've watched Full Metal Alchemist: Brotherhood, you should still read the manga, since it has more adventures that were deleted in Brotherhood.<br/><br/>This was quite fun. <br/>The story revolves aroun the Elric brothers, whom have performed the forbidden alchemical trnasmutation:<br/>Human transmutation.<br/>In an attempt to bring back their dead mother, Edward Elric loses his left leg, and his younger brother, Alphonse, loses his whole body. In a desperate attempt to bring back his brother, he sacrifices h</span>
  <span id="freeText9304090608021895180" style="display:none"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479049135i/21142615.jpg" width="800" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even if you've watched Full Metal Alchemist: Brotherhood, you should still read the manga, since it has more adventures that were deleted in Brotherhood.<br><br>This was quite fun. <br>The story revolves aroun the Elric brothers, whom have performed the forbidden alchemical trnasmutation:<br>Human transmutation.<br>In an attempt to bring back their dead mother, Edward Elric loses his left leg, and his younger brother, Alphonse, loses his whole body. In a desperate attempt to bring back his brother, he sacrifices his right arm to bind his brother's soul to a suit of armor.<br>The boys learn about the Philosophers Stone, a mystical item that greatly amplifies alchemical powers, and begin to search for it in order to restore their original bodies.<br>In order to have more access to the world, Ed becomes a State Alchemist, a dog of the military.<br><br>This volume collects their adventures in Leore, the mining town (which was barely include in Brotherhood.) and the train hijacking (completely removed from Brotherhood.)<br><br>I've watched the whole anime, so I know what's gonna happen, but the manga's still pretty good.<br>The arts understandable, the drawings fluid, and the fight scenes easy to understand. <br>It's also quite funny and will probably make you laugh.<br><br>If you want to start getting into manga, I suggest that you start with this.<br>Yes, it's Shounen, manga written for young boys, but FMA has a beautiful story. <br>It may seem childish and comedicmostmof the time, but, judging from the anime which was completely based on the manga, the story gets darker and more serious. It's even been called one of the saddest anime of all time. In of the best, at that matter. <br><br>Definitely recommend for sci-fi/fantasy/comedy/manga/action fans. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_182714538" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182714538" />
    <a title="Zoe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5753804-zoe"><img alt="Zoe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483305583p2/5753804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182714538?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe" href="/user/show/5753804-zoe">Zoe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182714538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6954727474123152733">Fullmetal Alchemist happens to be a one-of-a-kind in the manga genre. I mean, c'mon people: has ANYONE encountered such a brilliantly diverse series? Amongst a world of manga that is somewhat the same and unoriginal(enough with the vampire manga already, people!), Fullmetal Alchemist, or FMA as it is nicknamed by fans, stands out. <br/>This series is so well-known that I really shouldn't have to summarize it, but I will just in case you are one of the five or six people on this planet who have no ide</span>
  <span id="freeText6954727474123152733" style="display:none">Fullmetal Alchemist happens to be a one-of-a-kind in the manga genre. I mean, c'mon people: has ANYONE encountered such a brilliantly diverse series? Amongst a world of manga that is somewhat the same and unoriginal(enough with the vampire manga already, people!), Fullmetal Alchemist, or FMA as it is nicknamed by fans, stands out. <br />This series is so well-known that I really shouldn't have to summarize it, but I will just in case you are one of the five or six people on this planet who have no idea what this series is about:<br /><br />Twelve-year-old Edward Elric and his ten-year-old brother Alphonse have just lost their mother to a terminal illness. Abandoned by their father at an early age, they decide to learn the science of alchemy to try and resurrect her from the dead. Their attempt fails by a huge margin, leaving Ed minus two limbs and Al's soul glued to a seven foot tall suit of armor. Fast forward a few years: the two oddball brothers are on a search for the mythical Philosophers Stone, something that has been said to amplify alchemy, making it possible for the brothers to get their bodies back to normal. To aid him in his search, Ed has joined the military, becoming a State Alchemist in order to be granted access to the gigantic hordes of information that the state reserves for the 'dogs of the military,' in the hopes that there will be some kind of clue as to the stone's whereabouts.<br /><br />To be blunt, Fullmetal Alchemist is one of the best manga's that I have ever read, period. The characterization is done to perfection (it's IMPOSSIBLE not to like Ed and Al), the plot has enough twists and turns to keep your head spinning, and the art is unique and wonderful to look at. If you haven't already read this series, then what are you waiting for? I command you to read FMA and I dare you not to like it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6954727474123152733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Altogether a fun series I’ll definitely be continuing throughout this year!</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qIPqZOg7zpuBb8F05RBPjnfyUleXjHfM3hFvtMFzENaSpYO2U2UH8yZEdRUS5UVRoa21n1kB+auFbykFDDDiTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('l3hYduANFNskols/lb+Jrco5cVJmDa5oVuurOUV5gjOtXjGkW1Pds4OJ715iSoNyHGaWmqiAIA8Nle2IiDpwqQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11556815345654034967"><br/><b>Associated names :</b><br/>荒川弘美 (real name)<br/>ARAKAWA Hiromi<br/> <br/><b>Name (in native language) :</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13480257._' rel='nofollow noopener'>荒川弘</a><br/><br/><b>Zodiac :</b> Taurus<br/><br/><b>Blood type :</b> A<br/><br/>Her self-portrait is usually that of a bespectacled cow, as she was born and raised on a dairy farm in Hokkaido with three older sisters and a younger brother. She worked as a farmer for 8 years before moving to Tokyo.<br/><br/>Arakawa thought about being a manga artist "since [she] was little" and d</span>
  <span id="freeText11556815345654034967" style="display:none"><br /><b>Associated names :</b><br />荒川弘美 (real name)<br />ARAKAWA Hiromi<br /> <br /><b>Name (in native language) :</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13480257._" rel="nofollow noopener">荒川弘</a><br /><br /><b>Zodiac :</b> Taurus<br /><br /><b>Blood type :</b> A<br /><br />Her self-portrait is usually that of a bespectacled cow, as she was born and raised on a dairy farm in Hokkaido with three older sisters and a younger brother. She worked as a farmer for 8 years before moving to Tokyo.<br /><br />Arakawa thought about being a manga artist "since [she] was little" and during her school years, she would often draw on textbooks. After graduating high school, she took oil painting classes once a month for seven years while working on her family's farm. During this time, she also created dōjinshi manga with her friends and drew yonkoma for a magazine.<br /><br />Arakawa started out as Hiroyuki Eto's assistant writer for Mahōjin Guru Guru and a friend of Shakugan no Shana author Yashichirou Takahashi.<br /><br />Arakawa's career started with a work titled STRAY DOG, but she is best known for creating the Fullmetal Alchemist.<br /><br />For Fullmetal Alchemist manga, Arakawa had read alchemy-related books, which she found very complicated due to the fact that some books contradicted others. Arakawa was attracted more by the philosophical aspects than the practical aspects. For the Equivalent Exchange concept, she was inspired by the work of her parents who had a farm in Hokkaidō and always had to give all their effort in order to earn the money to eat. <br /><br />Friends with Akira Segami.<br /><br />Arakawa-san gave birth to a son in 2007.<br /><br />Kyu Aiya was an assistant of hers. Fusanosuke Inariya was possibly another assistant of hers.<br /><br />She received the Tezuka Osamu Cultural Award (New Artist Prize) 2011 for Fullmetal Alchemist.<br /><br />The Shinsei Prize was also awarded to Arakawa.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11556815345654034967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
